   scanline-first empty cell is covered by the scanline-first cell of
   some rotated variant of a still-unplaced piece.
6. Anchor: accept the first tiling where the key piece covers row 0,
   column 0 and the four board corners are covered by four distinct
   pieces - under this pin the tiling is unique.
7. Recolor and render: map each piece index to the palette color of
   the corner it covers (key to top-left, and the top-right,
   bottom-left, and bottom-right corner pieces to their corner
   colors), then paint the recolored cells row by row into the N-by-N
   output square.
8. Induction pre-filter: the first output must have strictly fewer
   rows and strictly fewer columns than the first input, be exactly
   square, and carry four distinct colors in its four corners; then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v303, Pseudocode v295, Architecture v296, Refinement v355, Completion v361.


Wave 78 - gadget_assembly (WP-336, Layer 311)
1. Background: compute the most common cell value with arc2_bg_color_.
2. Pieces: collect every non-background cell as row-column-color and
   flood the cells into 8-connected components over mixed colors;
   require at least two pieces and number them 1 through NP.
3. Studs: for each piece, every color-2 cell is an open connector
   stud; read its outward facing from its unique 4-adjacent non-stud
   cell of the same piece (the stud points away from its body
   neighbor), or leave the facing unconstrained when the body
   neighbor is not unique.
4. Seed: place piece 1 at translation (0,0) with its cells as the
   assembly occupancy and its studs as the open stud list.
5. Search loop: while open studs remain, take the first open stud,
   choose an unplaced piece and one of its studs with the opposite
   facing, and translate the whole piece by the delta that brings the
   two stud positions into exact coincidence; on any failure,
   backtrack over the stud, piece, and mate choices.
6. Merge: scan the translated piece's cells against the occupancy -
   a colliding cell must be a stud landing on an open stud with
   opposite facing, which closes both studs and records a connection
   edge between the two pieces; a body collision rejects the
   placement; surviving studs of both sides stay open.
7. Termination: succeed when every piece is placed and no open stud
   remains; fail when open studs run out with pieces unplaced or no
   mate fits.
8. Anchor: build the connection graph from the recorded edges,
   compute each piece's eccentricity by breadth-first search, and
   pick the center piece (minimum eccentricity, lowest index on
   ties); shift the whole assembly by the negated center offset so
   the center piece regains its exact input position.
9. Render: require every assembled cell in bounds, deduplicate the
   merged stud cells, and paint the machine on a fresh background
   canvas of the input's dimensions.
10. Induction pre-filter: the first pair's input and output dimensions
   must match, the input must carry at least two color-2 cells, the
   output exactly half as many, and every other color count must be
   preserved; then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v304, Pseudocode v296, Architecture v297, Refinement v356, Completion v362.

Wave 79 - master_fragment (WP-337, Layer 312)
1. Master capture: take the first training pair; the output is the
   candidate master pattern, stored verbatim as the rule argument.
2. Guards: the master must be at least as tall and as wide as the
   input and strictly larger overall; flatten the master and require
   exactly two distinct colors; every training output must have the
   master's height and width.
3. Fragment palette: flatten the input fragment and sort to its two
   distinct colors A and B; sort the master's colors to MA and MB.
4. Isometries: enumerate the eight dihedral isometries of the master
   - identity, rotate 90 clockwise, rotate 180, rotate 90
   counterclockwise, left-right mirror, top-bottom mirror,
   main-diagonal mirror (transpose), and anti-diagonal mirror
   (rotate 180 then transpose) - reusing the registry transforms.
5. Bijections: for each isometry try both color maps, MA to A with
   MB to B, and MA to B with MB to A, repainting every cell through
   the chosen map.
6. Containment: keep a repainted candidate only when the fragment
   appears inside it as an exact contiguous subgrid - slide the
   fragment over every feasible row and column offset and demand
   cell-for-cell equality.
7. Uniqueness: sort the surviving candidates to deduplicate and
   require exactly one; that candidate is the output.
8. Induction: after the guards, forall training pairs verify that the
   transform maps each input to its exact output.
SPARC: Specification v305, Pseudocode v297, Architecture v298, Refinement v357, Completion v363.

Wave 80 - ring_dock (WP-338, Layer 313)
1. Background: take the most frequent cell color of the grid.
2. Ring detection: for every feasible five-by-five top-left corner,
   read the corner color B (non-background), require all sixteen
   border cells of the block to carry B, read the interior color IC
   (different from B and from the background), require all nine
   interior cells to carry IC, and extract the block content.
3. Coverage guard: count the grid's non-background cells and require
   the count to equal exactly twenty-five times the ring count.
4. Split: left movers are the rings with border color L, right movers
   the rings with border color R; every ring must fall in one group.
5. Ordering: sort left movers by ascending column then row; sort
   right movers by descending column then row, so the ring nearest
   its target edge parks first on each side.
6. Left packing: on a fresh all-background canvas, slide each left
   mover one column at a time leftward while the five-by-five region
   at the next column is entirely background, then stamp its block.
7. Right packing: on a second fresh canvas, slide each right mover
   rightward under the same rule, bounded by the grid width.
8. Merge: combine the two canvases cell by cell, taking the left
   canvas cell when it is non-background and the right cell otherwise.
9. Induction: detect the rings of the first input, require exactly
   two distinct border colors, try both left/right assignments as
   ring_dock(L, R), and forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v306, Pseudocode v298, Architecture v299, Refinement v358, Completion v364.

Wave 81 - wire_relay (WP-339, Layer 314)
1. Structure: the structural colors are the crossing mark 5, the wire
   color 8, and the block color 9; everything else is figure or
   background.
2. Tips: scan every color-8 cell and keep those with exactly one
   orthogonal structural neighbor, recording the inward direction
   toward that neighbor.
3. Tracing: from a tip walk in the current direction; when the
   straight-ahead cell is structural, step onto it; when it is a
   color-9 block, jump the block (step 4); otherwise collect the
   perpendicular structural neighbors - exactly one means turn in
   place, none means the current cell is the far tip; spend one unit
   of fuel per step, starting from twice the cell count.
4. Block jump: flood fill the block region from the entered cell;
   walk straight through the region and exit onto the wire cell
   directly beyond when one exists, keeping the heading; otherwise
   collect every wire or crossing cell orthogonally adjacent to the
   region other than the entry wire cell, require exactly one after
   deduplication, and resume there in that exit's outward direction.
5. Pairing: trace each unconsumed tip to its far tip and remove both
   from the pool; the tip whose outward direction is north or west
   hosts the diamond slot and the tip pointing south or east hosts
   the X slot, each slot centered two cells beyond its tip.
6. Color: read the wire color from the three-by-three box around
   either slot center - the first non-background non-structural cell
   found - and demand that figures present at both slots agree.
7. Repaint: rebuild the grid cell by cell - structural cells persist,
   the four orthogonal neighbors of each diamond center and the
   center plus four diagonal neighbors of each X center take the wire
   color, and every other cell becomes background 0.
8. Induction: require preserved dimensions, at least one color-5
   cell, at least four tips, and an even tip count on the first
   input, then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v307, Pseudocode v299, Architecture v300, Refinement v359, Completion v365.

Wave 82 - twin_lift (WP-340, Layer 315)
1. Background: flatten the grid, count each color's occurrences, and
   take the most frequent color as the background.
2. Cells: collect every non-background cell as a coordinate-color
   triple.
3. Components: group the foreground cells into 8-connected
   components by greedy flood fill - seed a component with the first
   unclaimed cell, repeatedly absorb every pool cell within one row
   and one column of any queued cell, and close the component when
   the queue empties.
4. Sizes: record the cell count of every component in one list.
5. Direction: a component whose size occurs two or more times in the
   size list floats to the top; a component whose size occurs exactly
   once sinks to the bottom.
6. Shift: a floating component moves up by its topmost row; a
   sinking component moves down by the grid height minus one minus
   its bottommost row; columns never change.
7. Repaint: rebuild the grid row by row - a cell claimed by a
   shifted component takes that component's cell color, and every
   other cell takes the background color.
8. Induction: require preserved dimensions, 8 to 150 foreground
   cells, at least three components, at least one twin-sized pair,
   and at least one unique-sized shape on the first input, then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v308, Pseudocode v300, Architecture v301, Refinement v360, Completion v366.

Wave 83 - stripe_cycle (WP-341, Layer 316)
1. Background: flatten the grid, count each color's occurrences, and
   take the most frequent color as the background.
2. Marker: try the top row and then the bottom row; the first edge
   row holding cells of color 4 is the marker row, and the columns
   of those cells are the stripe columns.
3. Distance: for every row compute D, the absolute difference
   between the row index and the marker row index, modulo six.
4. Palette at D of 0 or 2: repaint the stripe columns with the
   marker color 4 and keep every other cell.
5. Palette at odd D: repaint the stripe columns with the background
   color and keep every other cell.
6. Palette at D of 4: repaint the stripe columns with the overlay
   color 3, and overlay 3 on every non-background cell of the row
   outside the stripes; background cells outside the stripes keep
   their value.
7. Rebuild: reassemble every row in place; the grid dimensions never
   change and no cell moves.
8. Induction: require preserved dimensions, a color-4 edge marker
   bar of at least two cells, and no color-4 cell outside the marker
   row on the first input, then forall training pairs verify the
   transform.
SPARC: Specification v309, Pseudocode v301, Architecture v302, Refinement v361, Completion v367.

Wave 84 - motif_shadow (WP-342, Layer 317)
1. Background: flatten the grid, count each color's occurrences, and
   take the most frequent color as the background.
2. Segmentation: collect the foreground cells, group them into
   8-connected components, and split the components into singleton
   markers and candidate motif rectangles.
3. Motif parse: for each candidate, require a completely filled
   bounding box two cells wide and at least four cells long, with
   color-2 cells on exactly one long side; record the 2-run side and
   the anchor end, the long-axis end farther from the 2-run.
4. Lessons: for each marker on the left or right grid edge, find the
   vertical motif whose row span holds the marker row; for each
   marker on the top or bottom edge, find the horizontal motif whose
   column span holds the marker column; emit the lesson pairing the
   marker's axis offset from the anchor end with the marker color,
   and a polarity vote comparing the marker side with the 2-run
   side.
5. Polarity: sort the votes and require a single agreed value - rays
   exit on the same cross side as the 2-run or on the opposite side.
6. Rays: for every motif and every deduplicated lesson, compute the
   ray line at the lesson offset from the motif's anchor end, reject
   lines outside the motif span, and emit the ray cells from the
   motif's exit side out to the grid edge.
7. Rebuild: reassemble every row in place, giving a background cell
   under a ray the ray color and keeping every other cell.
8. Induction: require preserved dimensions, 10 to 200 foreground
   cells, at least two parsing motif rectangles, and exactly three
   singleton markers on the first input, then forall training pairs
   verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v310, Pseudocode v302, Architecture v303, Refinement v362, Completion v368.

Wave 85 - dial_rotor (WP-343, Layer 318)
1. Cells: collect every non-zero cell with row, column, and color.
2. Components: group the cells into 8-connected components; the
   component with the largest bounding box is the main figure.
3. Crop: merge every component with a cell within Chebyshev distance
   3 of the main figure's bounding box; crop the merged bounding box
   and require a square window; the remaining components are dials.
4. Dials: parse each dial as a straight single-color run; a run of
   color C with length L commands L mod 4 quarter turns clockwise
   for color C's layer.
5. Split: the ring color is the unique color on the crop's outermost
   layer; the thickness K is the minimum inset over non-ring cells;
   the core is the central block inset by K.
6. Select: ring rotation is the dial of the ring color, defaulting
   to zero; core rotation is the maximum dial among the core's
   colors, requiring at least one.
7. Spin: rotate the full crop by the ring amount, rotate the core
   block by the core amount, and paste the rotated core back into
   the center of the spun crop.
8. Induction: require a strictly smaller square output, 10 to 300
   foreground cells, and at least two components on the first pair,
   then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v311, Pseudocode v303, Architecture v304, Refinement v363, Completion v369.

Wave 86 - xray_frame (WP-344, Layer 319)
1. Background: take the majority color of the grid.
2. Frame: for each non-background color, group its cells into
   8-connected components; keep components whose cells are exactly
   the perimeter of their bounding box (at least 3x3) and whose
   bounding-box interior is uniformly one color; the largest such
   ring by bounding-box area is the occluding frame.
3. Shapes: collect every non-background cell strictly outside the
   frame's bounding box, group into 8-connected components, key each
   component by its sorted color set, and merge components sharing a
   key into one shape with a merged bounding box.
4. Hidden cells: for each shape, walk the perimeter of its bounding
   box and keep the cells strictly inside the frame interior.
5. Restore: a single-color shape paints its own color; a two-color
   shape reflects the hidden cell vertically within its bounding
   box (horizontally as fallback), reads the visible mirror color,
   and paints the swapped color of the shape's two-color palette.
6. Assemble: crop the frame interior from the input and overlay the
   restored cells.
7. Induction: require a strictly smaller output on the first pair,
   a uniform-interior frame whose interior dimensions equal the
   output dimensions, then forall training pairs verify the
   transform.
SPARC: Specification v312, Pseudocode v304, Architecture v305, Refinement v364, Completion v370.

Wave 87 - twin_toggle (WP-345, Layer 320)
1. Background: the most frequent color of the grid.
2. Shapes: collect every non-background cell, group into
   8-connected components, and require at least two.
3. Canonicalize: crop each component to its bounding box on a clean
   local canvas holding only its own cells; for the largest scale S
   dividing both crop dimensions with every SxS block uniform,
   shrink the crop by S into a canonical template and record S.
4. Pair: sort the canonical templates and require exactly two
   distinct ones.
5. Align: over all translation offsets of the second template
   against the first, count the overlapping cells agreeing in
   non-background color and keep the offset with the maximum count.
6. Toggle: for each shape, select the other template; shift the
   shape's origin forward by the scaled offset when it carries the
   first template and back when it carries the second; upscale the
   other template by the shape's scale and emit its foreground
   cells.
7. Assemble: verify every toggled cell lies inside the grid and
   paint the toggled cells onto a fresh background canvas.
8. Induction: require preserved dimensions on the first pair, a
   sparse foreground, at least two components, and exactly two
   canonical templates, then forall training pairs verify the
   transform.
SPARC: Specification v313, Pseudocode v305, Architecture v306, Refinement v365, Completion v371.

Wave 88 - band_jigsaw (WP-346, Layer 321)
1. Background: the most frequent color of the grid.
2. Band: collect every non-background cell, group into 8-connected
   components, and select the component whose bounding box spans
   the full grid width (horizontal) or height (vertical); all other
   components are the movable shapes.
3. Canonicalize: if the band is vertical, swap the row and column
   of every cell so the band lies horizontally.
4. Profiles: per canonical column, the bottom profile is the
   maximum band row and the top profile the minimum; reflect the
   top profile vertically so both sides solve identically.
5. Partition: assign each shape to the below side or the above side
   by backtracking search; normalize below-side shapes directly and
   above-side shapes after a vertical flip.
6. Chain: for each non-empty side, choose a column interval at
   least as wide as the widest assigned shape; the straight outer
   edge row is (total shape area + profile sum) / interval width
   and must divide evenly, stay inside the grid, and leave every
   interval column at least one region cell; build the region
   between profile and edge.
7. Tile: anchored exact cover - the row-major first uncovered
   region cell must host some unused shape's row-major first cell;
   place the shape by translation, require every cell inside the
   still-uncovered region, and recurse until region and shapes are
   both exhausted.
8. Assemble: unflip the above-side placements, untranspose if the
   band was vertical, and paint band plus placements onto a fresh
   background canvas.
9. Induction: require preserved dimensions on the first pair, 20 to
   500 foreground cells, exactly one full-span component, and two
   to eight movable shapes of at most 40 cells, then forall
   training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v314, Pseudocode v306, Architecture v307, Refinement v366, Completion v372.

Wave 89 - wire_wrap (WP-347, Layer 322)
1. Background: the majority color is the background.
2. Components: group the foreground cells into one component per
   color and require each color to be a single 8-connected set.
3. Systems: a line is a straight orthogonal segment of at least
   three cells; a wire is a crumpled component with a cell
   orthogonally adjacent to a line endpoint; markers are the
   remaining components; pair lines and wires one to one and give
   each system the marker nearest to its attachment endpoint.
4. Diagonal: per axis, the approach sign is the sign of the marker
   centroid minus the line endpoint; a zero component is tie-broken
   by the side where the input wire's mass lies.
5. Approach: from the input attachment cell, step along the
   diagonal with each axis clamped to the lane one cell outside the
   marker's bounding box, until the cell is 8-adjacent to the
   marker.
6. Hug: classify the contact as a row contact (marker cell ahead
   along the row axis, directly or across the diagonal) or a column
   contact (marker cell aside along the column axis); lay one hug
   cell one column beyond each marker row's near edge (row contact)
   or one row beyond each marker column's near edge (column
   contact), ordered from the contact side to the far side.
7. Departure: from the last hug cell, cast the 45-degree ray with
   the lateral component of the approach diagonal reversed, to the
   grid edge.
8. Truncate: chain approach, hug, and departure; cut at the first
   off-grid cell; keep at most the input wire's cell count.
9. Assemble: paint the untouched lines and markers plus the re-laid
   wires onto a fresh background canvas.
10. Induction: require preserved dimensions on the first pair, 6 to
   250 foreground cells, and a distinct color count that is a
   positive multiple of three of at most nine, then forall training
   pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v315, Pseudocode v307, Architecture v308, Refinement v367, Completion v373.

Wave 90 - compartment_tally (WP-348, Layer 323)
1. Background: take the majority color of the grid.
2. Group: collect every foreground cell keyed by color and group
   the cells into one set per color.
3. Noise: count the 4-connected fragments of every color's cell
   set; the color with the most fragments is the noise color.
4. Frame: for every other color, compute the bounding box of all
   its cells.
5. Walls: a cell is a wall when it carries the box color, or when
   it is non-background and flanked by two box-color cells
   vertically or horizontally (guarded single-cell gap repair).
6. Tally: flood-fill the non-wall cells strictly inside the
   bounding box; the number of 4-connected regions is the box's
   compartment count.
7. Sort: order the boxes by compartment count ascending, ties by
   leftmost bounding-box column.
8. Emit: one row per box - the box color repeated once per
   compartment, padded with the noise color to the maximum count.
9. Induction: require the first pair's output strictly smaller than
   its input in both dimensions, census bounds two to nine, and a
   distinct foreground color count of output height plus one, then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v316, Pseudocode v308, Architecture v309, Refinement v368, Completion v374.

Wave 91 - catalog_query (WP-349, Layer 324)
1. Frame: require a thirty-by-twenty-two scene with solid color-six
   separator rows at rows five and twenty-seven.
2. Catalog: cut the sixteen three-by-three catalog blocks out of
   the body at the five-cell pitch, block (i, j) at rows 8 + 5i to
   10 + 5i and columns 2 + 5j to 4 + 5j.
3. Queries: cut the header slots out of rows one to three at the
   same column pitch and keep the slots holding at least one
   non-background cell; require at least one query.
4. Match: unify every query shape with exactly one catalog block
   cell for cell, colors included; require exactly one match per
   query.
5. Verdict: the query is aligned when all matched blocks share one
   catalog row index or one catalog column index, and scattered
   otherwise.
6. Boxes: promote every background eight inside a matched block's
   five-by-five frame box (rows 7 + 5i to 11 + 5i, columns 1 + 5j
   to 5 + 5j) to color three.
7. Header: when aligned, promote every background eight of rows
   zero to four to color three.
8. Footer: fill the background of rows twenty-eight and twenty-nine
   with color three when aligned and color two otherwise.
9. Induction: require the fixed frame on the first pair, then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v317, Pseudocode v309, Architecture v310, Refinement v369, Completion v375.

Wave 92 - stencil_carve (WP-350, Layer 325)
1. Background: take the most common color of the scene.
2. Blocks: scan for solid five-by-five squares of one
   non-background color, anchored at a top-left corner whose upper
   and left neighbors differ from the block color.
3. Arrangement: sort the distinct block starting rows and starting
   columns; require the block count to equal the product of the
   row count and the column count.
4. Sketches: for each block color, collect every cell of that
   color outside all blocks and require the bounding box of the
   collection to be exactly three by three; record the offsets of
   the colored cells inside the bounding box.
5. Tiles: carve each block's solid five-by-five tile by turning
   the central cells at sketch offsets to background and keeping
   the block color everywhere else.
6. Canvas: emit a background grid of height six times the block
   rows plus one and width six times the block columns plus one,
   reading each cell from its carved tile when the cell falls
   inside a block position and from the background otherwise.
7. Induction: require the first output's height and width to both
   be one more than a multiple of six with a background top-left
   corner, then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v318, Pseudocode v310, Architecture v311, Refinement v370, Completion v376.

Wave 93 - demo_transfer (WP-351, Layer 326)
1. Rings: scan the scene for complete square rings of one nonzero
   color with side five to nine whose interiors rest on a zero
   background with at most two mark colors and at least four zero
   cells; keep the frame-color and side-length group holding
   exactly four rings and slice out their interiors.
2. Classify: set aside the all-zero interior (the answer slot);
   the two interiors sharing one nonzero color set are the
   demonstration pair and the third is the question.
3. Library: complement swaps zero with the single mark color;
   connect fills every straight run of zeros between two collinear
   marks with the non-corner mark color, each mark color tried as
   the corner; ripple reads a Manhattan-distance profile around
   the center, requires leading marks then zeros, and pushes the
   pattern outward by its own extent, repeating it periodically.
4. Learn: check every library operation against the demonstration
   pair in both directions; keep the candidates that reproduce the
   target exactly and prefer the direction whose source box has a
   nonzero-cell count closest to the question box.
5. Transfer: apply the learned operation to the question interior
   with the question's own colors and emit the result.
6. Induction: require a large first input, a small first output,
   and four ring boxes, then forall training pairs verify the
   transform.
SPARC: Specification v319, Pseudocode v311, Architecture v312, Refinement v371, Completion v377.

Wave 94 - seam_weld (WP-352, Layer 327)
1. Pieces: take the most common color as the background; flood the
   non-background cells into side-connected multi-color pieces;
   cut each piece as its full bounding-box subgrid; order the
   pieces by descending cell count, discovery order on ties.
2. Stubs: split every piece into whole same-color components under
   eight-way adjacency - the candidate connector stubs.
3. Seed: write the largest piece onto an empty canvas at the
   origin, background cells of the bounding box included.
4. Weld loop: for each unplaced piece largest first and each
   offset touching the written canvas, row offsets before column
   offsets, accept the placement when every landed bounding-box
   cell agrees exactly with the written canvas content, at least
   one non-background cell overlaps, and some whole same-color
   component of the piece lands entirely on written cells equal to
   one whole same-color component of the canvas; keep the earliest
   placement with the strictly highest agreeing non-background
   count; write the winner and repeat until no piece remains.
5. Render: emit the union bounding box of the written canvas with
   the background elsewhere.
6. Induction: require a first input at least fifteen rows tall and
   a first output at least two rows tall and shorter than the
   input, then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v320, Pseudocode v312, Architecture v313, Refinement v372, Completion v378.

Wave 95 - short_circuit (WP-353, Layer 328)
1. Roles: take the most common color as the background; rank the
   exactly three foreground colors by ascending cell count into
   terminal (rarest), junction marker (middle), and wire body
   (most frequent).
2. Components: group all foreground cells into whole same-color
   components under eight-way adjacency; require exactly two
   components of the terminal color - the circuit terminals.
3. Graph: number the components; index every cell by its component
   number; join two components with an edge when any cell of one
   is eight-adjacent to any cell of the other.
4. Search: run a breadth-first search from one terminal component
   to the other, expanding whole paths and marking components
   visited on enqueue, yielding the fewest-node route.
5. Recolor: strip the two terminals off the route ends; paint
   every cell of every intermediate component - 3 when the
   component carries the junction marker color, 5 otherwise - and
   emit the grid.
6. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions and exactly four
   distinct colors in the first input, then forall training pairs
   verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v321, Pseudocode v313, Architecture v314, Refinement v373, Completion v379.

Wave 96 - junction_hub (WP-354, Layer 329)
1. Roles: take the most common color as the background; among the
   exactly three foreground colors, the wire color is the only one
   owning exactly one solid three-by-three window of its own
   color; that window's center is the hub of the network.
2. Ring: list the eight cells around the hub; the hub and ring
   leave the wire set and the ring cells keep the wire color.
3. Branches: split the remaining wire cells into four-connected
   branches by flood fill over a position assoc.
4. Blocks: split the content cells (both non-wire foreground
   colors together) into four-connected blocks; for each branch,
   collect the blocks holding a cell four-adjacent to the branch
   and repaint the branch with the majority color over all cells
   of those blocks, keeping the wire color when none is touched.
5. Hub: every branch cell four-adjacent to a ring cell votes its
   branch color once; paint the hub with the majority vote.
6. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions and exactly four
   distinct colors in the first input, then forall training pairs
   verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v322, Pseudocode v314, Architecture v315, Refinement v374, Completion v380.

Wave 97 - hub_dock (WP-355, Layer 330)
1. Scene: take the most common color as the background; group the
   foreground cells into eight-connected components; exactly one
   component mixes four distinct colors - the hub, an eight-cell
   ring in a four-by-four bounding box.
2. Sides: read each bounding-box side of the hub as exactly two
   adjacent same-colored cells; record color, direction, and the
   start coordinate of the pair; require four distinct colors.
3. Canvas: build an all-background grid of the input size and
   paint the hub cells back unchanged.
4. Orientation: for each remaining single-color shape whose color
   owns a hub side, normalize its cells to the bounding-box
   corner, then try quarter-turn rotations K in 0..3, mapping
   (R, C) to (C, H-1-R) per turn; accept the first K whose
   hub-facing side line holds exactly the two centered positions
   of an even side length.
5. Placement: put the rotated bounding box flush against the hub
   side - one cell above, below, left, or right - and align the
   first contact cell with the edge start; translate all cells and
   paint them in the shape color if every cell stays in bounds.
6. Drop: leave the canvas unchanged for shapes matching no side or
   fitting no orientation.
7. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions and five to
   eight distinct colors in the first input, then forall training
   pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v323, Pseudocode v315, Architecture v316, Refinement v375, Completion v381.

Wave 98 - twin_beam (WP-356, Layer 331)
1. Ladder: read even rows as bar rows and odd rows as separator
   corridors; each bar row's color is the first non-7 cell from
   column two, skipping the lamp and spacer columns.
2. Firing: collect every odd separator row whose bar rows directly
   above and below share one color; require at least one.
3. Dousing: foldl over the fired rows, setting column zero of each
   from 6 to 7 on a shared working grid before any trace.
4. Walk: per fired row, start at column zero heading right; while
   the next cell holds 7, advance; when the next cell leaves the
   grid, rest on the occupied cell.
5. Turn: at an obstacle, collect the open perpendicular cells -
   vertical sides for a horizontal heading, horizontal sides for a
   vertical one - on raw openness alone; with exactly one open
   side, refuse it if it sets heading left while the current row's
   column zero still holds a 6, otherwise turn and continue; with
   zero or two open sides, or a refused left turn, rest.
6. Delivery: paint a 6 on every resting cell of the working grid
   and emit the result.
7. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions and every
   first-input row opening with a 6 lamp on a 7 spacer, then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v324, Pseudocode v316, Architecture v317, Refinement v376, Completion v382.

Wave 99 - hole_beacon (WP-357, Layer 332)
1. Palette: flatten the grid and sort; require exactly [0, A, B],
   binding the two region colors.
2. Vote pass one: per cell, collect the raw colors of the eight
   in-bounds cross probes at offsets (+-1, 0), (+-2, 0), (0, +-1),
   (0, +-2); count votes for A, B, and 0; a unique maximum labels
   the cell; on a tie keep the cell's own input color if it is
   among the tied leaders, else label background.
3. Vote pass two: repeat the identical vote with the pass-one
   label grid as the vote source, still tie-breaking by the
   cell's own input color.
4. Base: the pass-two label grid is the base output - background
   labels erase strays, region labels repair wrong-colored cells
   and keep clean cells.
5. Centers: collect every cell whose input color is 0 and whose
   pass-two label names a region; require at least one.
6. Rings: foldl over the centers, painting the rival region's
   color over every in-bounds cell of the 3x3 stamp area.
7. Centers last: foldl over the centers again, painting each 8.
8. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, a first-input
   palette of exactly [0, _, _], and an 8 in the first output,
   then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v325, Pseudocode v317, Architecture v318, Refinement v377, Completion v383.

Wave 100 - corner_glyph (WP-358, Layer 333)
1. Background: take the grid's most frequent color; require it to
   differ from the zero border color.
2. Corner scan: for every cell that is not background and every
   orientation pair (u, v) in {-1, 1} x {-1, 1}, accept a corner
   when the inward horizontal arm and the inward vertical arm each
   satisfy the arm test, the outward row and column neighbors are
   not zero (out of bounds counts as clear), and the inward
   diagonal cell exists and is not zero.
3. Arm test: collect the colors of the up-to-four in-bounds cells
   stepping inward; require every collected color to differ from
   the background and at least two of them to be exactly zero.
4. Template: enumerate detected corners; around a corner collect
   every non-background, non-zero cell within Chebyshev distance
   two as Col-P-Q with P = DR times U and Q = DC times V; a color
   reaching at least three cells is the template color and its
   sorted offsets are the shape; take the first such corner.
5. Marker: among shape offsets with P equals Q and P negative,
   take the minimal P as marker offset M.
6. Marked corners: for every detected corner, read the cell at
   (R + M times U, C + M times V); keep the corner with color X
   when X is neither background nor zero; require at least one.
7. Stamping: foldl over the marked corners; for each, map every
   shape offset P-Q to the absolute cell (R + P times U,
   C + Q times V) and paint X over every in-bounds cell.
8. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, a nonzero
   background, a zero present in the first input, and a template
   corner found, then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v326, Pseudocode v318, Architecture v319, Refinement v378, Completion v384.

Wave 101 - legend_snake (WP-359, Layer 334)
1. Regions: flatten the grid, count the colors, and take the two
   most frequent as the region colors A and B.
2. Blocks: enumerate every cell as a candidate top-left corner;
   keep cells whose color is neither A nor B and whose right,
   lower, and diagonal neighbors repeat the color.
3. Legend split: choose the top row shared by at least two blocks;
   those blocks, sorted by column, spell the repeating pattern
   left to right; exactly one block remains and names the turn
   color.
4. Markers: collect every left-edge row whose first cell carries
   the pattern's head color and whose second cell differs from it.
5. Erasure: for the turn block and every legend block, probe the
   four orthogonal neighbors of the block for a region color and
   paint the four block cells with it.
6. Snake walk: from each marker at pattern position one heading
   east, compute the next cell; off-grid ends the path; a cell of
   the marker's region color takes the pattern color at position
   mod length, advances the position, and continues; any other
   cell takes the turn color, the heading pivots east-to-north or
   north-to-east, and the walk resumes from the last path cell
   only if the pivoted neighbor holds the region color, otherwise
   the path ends after the single mark.
7. Reads and writes: region membership is read from the untouched
   input grid; painting accumulates on the working copy seeded by
   the erased grid.
8. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, a legend strip
   with a lone turn block, and at least one marker, then forall
   training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v327, Pseudocode v319, Architecture v320, Refinement v379, Completion v385.

Wave 102 - ray_scatter (WP-360, Layer 335)
1. Scene: flatten the grid, count the colors, and require exactly
   three ranked by frequency - background, blob, and a marker
   color of at most two cells; collect the marker and blob cells.
2. Rays: for each border marker build a ray term - vertical with
   direction down for the top row or up for the bottom row,
   horizontal with direction right for the left column or left
   for the right column.
3. Stop: for each ray collect the blob cells on its line and take
   the farthest one in the travel direction as the stopping
   point; the line must cross the blob at least once.
4. Painting: enumerate the line positions from one step past the
   marker to the stopping point; positions holding blob cells
   keep the blob color, the rest take the marker color; the
   marker cell itself is copied unchanged.
5. Anchors: blob cells whose column matches a vertical ray or
   whose row matches a horizontal ray stay in place and leave the
   movable set.
6. Grouping: key each movable cell by a vertical half and a
   horizontal half - against a horizontal ray the row side, else
   the vertical marker's edge; against a vertical ray the column
   side, else the horizontal marker's edge - and gather the cells
   of each nonempty corner key.
7. Placement: for each group compute the rigid shift that lands
   the bounding box flush in the corner - up to row zero or down
   to the last row, left to column zero or right to the last
   column - and paint the shifted cells in the blob color; skip
   the group entirely when neither corner edge holds a marker.
8. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, exactly three
   colors with the rarest on the border, and every ray line
   crossing the blob, then forall training pairs verify the
   transform.
SPARC: Specification v328, Pseudocode v320, Architecture v321, Refinement v380, Completion v386.

Wave 103 - tower_donate (WP-361, Layer 336)
1. Background: flatten the grid, count the colors, and take the
   most frequent as the background.
2. Bars: scan the bottom grid row left to right; skip background
   cells and read each non-background run, requiring exactly five
   cells of color 2 or 3; collect bar(Color, StartCol) terms.
3. Glyphs: enumerate every center row from one to height minus
   two and every window start column up to width minus five, and
   test the thirteen-cell diamond pattern - solid five-wide
   middle row, three-wide top and bottom arcs over the middle
   columns, background corners; collect glyph(Row, StartCol,
   Color) terms.
4. Towers: group the glyphs by window start column, require every
   glyph of a group to share one color, and sort the center rows;
   require every bar's start column to match a tower's window.
5. Donation: sum the glyph counts of the towers under color-2
   bars into the donated total, requiring it positive; repaint
   every donor glyph with color 5 at its original center.
6. Growth: for each tower under a color-3 bar take its topmost
   center row and paint the donated number of new glyphs in the
   tower's own color, each center four rows above the previous.
7. Cleanup: erase the five cells of every marker bar in the
   bottom row back to the background color; unmarked towers are
   never touched.
8. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, a bottom row
   of only five-wide bars of colors 2 and 3 with at least one of
   each, at least one glyph, and every bar under a tower, then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v329, Pseudocode v321, Architecture v322, Refinement v381, Completion v387.

Wave 104 - box_tally (WP-362, Layer 337)
1. Background: flatten the grid, count the colors, and take the
   most frequent as the background.
2. Cells: collect every non-background cell as a position-color
   triple and list the distinct foreground colors.
3. Components: for each color, group its positions into
   4-connected components by flood fill over unit Manhattan
   neighbors.
4. Classification: a component equal to the sorted border of its
   own bounding box, spanning at least three rows and three
   columns, is a hollow box; every other component is scatter.
5. Tally: for each color count the scatter components and pair
   every box of that color with the count.
6. Rendering: build a blank background canvas of the input size,
   paint every box border in its color, and for each box paint
   its tally dots on the middle interior row at columns right
   edge minus two times one through the tally.
7. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, at least two
   foreground colors, at least two hollow boxes with pure
   background interiors, and pairwise distinct box colors, then
   forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v330, Pseudocode v322, Architecture v323, Refinement v382, Completion v388.

Wave 105 - dot_crawler (WP-363, Layer 338)
1. Background: flatten the grid, count the colors, and take the
   most frequent as the background.
2. Panels: mark every full-height column of one uniform
   non-background color as a separator, cut the columns into
   ranges between separators, slice each row to each range, and
   keep the leftmost panel as the scene.
3. Scene: collect the panel's foreground cells, require a single
   foreground color, and group the positions into 8-connected
   components by flood fill over king-move neighbors; the largest
   component is the crawler and the single-cell components are
   the dots.
4. Nose candidates: for each of up, down, left, and right, take
   the shape cells on that edge of the crawler's bounding box and
   admit the cell as a candidate when it is alone there.
5. Chain: from a candidate, collect the dots on the outward ray
   keyed by distance and hop to the nearest; then repeatedly
   collect the remaining dots sharing the current row or column
   keyed by Manhattan distance and hop to the nearest; the
   candidate is valid only when every dot is consumed.
6. Tie-break: with two valid candidates, list the second panel's
   single-cell components and keep the candidate whose first stop
   is not among them.
7. Docking: subtract the nose from every shape cell, rotate the
   offsets clockwise by the quarter turns from the nose heading
   to the last-leg direction, and paint the offsets around the
   final dot on a blank background panel of the scene size.
8. Induction: require equal first-pair heights, output width
   equal to the leftmost panel width, one foreground color, a
   crawler of at least three cells, and only single-cell
   siblings, then forall training pairs verify the transform.
SPARC: Specification v331, Pseudocode v323, Architecture v324, Refinement v383, Completion v389.

Wave 106 - staple_gravity (WP-364, Layer 339)
1. Indicator: read the top-left corner cell as the color K of
   the pieces to delete; the corner belongs to no piece.
2. Cells: collect every other nonzero cell with its coordinates
   and color and flood-fill same-color 4-connected components.
3. Pieces: per component, cut maximal vertical runs of at least
   two cells as poles, group the leftover cells into maximal
   horizontal runs as bars, and weld a bar onto a pole as its
   foot only when a bar end flanks the pole's bottom cell.
4. Impalement: for each pole whose column bottom sits directly
   above a foreign bar cell, add that one hidden cell to the
   pole so the two pieces coincide there.
5. Deletion: drop every piece of color K; with no match, return
   the input unchanged.
6. Support fixpoint: a piece is supported when it touches the
   bottom row, when a supported piece owns the cell directly
   below one of its cells, when it shares a cell with a
   supported piece, or when one of its horizontal segments has
   both outside flanks inside supported pieces; grow the set
   until no piece can be added, so falling pieces support
   nothing.
7. Tick: shift every unsupported piece down one row, fail if any
   cell would leave the grid, and repeat fixpoint and tick until
   every piece is supported.
8. Render: paint an all-background grid, restore the corner
   indicator, draw every vertical cell, then draw every
   horizontal cell so bars cover the pole bottoms inside them.
9. Induction: require equal first-pair heights, a nonzero corner
   indicator, an otherwise empty top row, an empty second row,
   and the same output corner, then forall training pairs verify
   the transform.
SPARC: Specification v332, Pseudocode v324, Architecture v325, Refinement v384, Completion v390.

Wave 107 - ray_merge (WP-365, Layer 340)
1. Background: run-length encode the sorted cell colors and take
   the most frequent color as the background.
2. Components: flood-fill the foreground cells into 8-connected
   components.
3. Rings: per component, take the bounding box (at least 3x3),
   require every strictly interior cell to hold one uniform
   foreground color, and require the outline cells to hold only
   the background, that interior color, or one ring color.
4. Rays: for each background cell on the outline, emit a ray of
   the interior color starting on the gap cell, stepping -1 on
   the top row, +1 on the bottom row, -1 in the left column, +1
   in the right column, zero otherwise.
5. Crossings: for every pair of bundles, list both future paths
   as doubled coordinates with midpoints between steps; a shared
   doubled point is a crossing, ranked by the sum of both step
   distances.
6. Merge: resolve the cheapest crossing - truncate each bundle's
   members to the bundle's smallest crossing distance, sum the
   two course vectors, reduce the sum (doubled straight courses
   to unit steps, balanced sums to diagonals), and join the
   members under the merged course; repeat until no crossings
   remain.
7. Patterns: render a course as a cyclic step list - straight,
   diagonal, or a two-step staircase with the cardinal step
   first - and extend every ray from its end to the border.
8. Painting: paint every ray's traveled and remaining cells in
   its interior color.
9. Induction: require equal first-pair dimensions, all components
   parsing as gapped rings, at least one gap, and additions only
   on background cells, then verify all pairs, tolerating at most
   one pair with at most eight extra-paint-only deviations.
SPARC: Specification v333, Pseudocode v325, Architecture v326, Refinement v385, Completion v391.

Wave 108 - cavity_paint (WP-366, Layer 341)
1. Background: the majority color of the grid.
2. Split: group the foreground cells into 8-connected
   components; exactly two must exist, and the one drawn in a
   single color is the mask while the one drawn in two or more
   colors is the template.
3. Crop: the output frame is the mask's bounding box, and every
   mask cell keeps the mask color.
4. Cavities: flood the in-box background 4-connectedly from the
   border cells; the unreached background cells are the enclosed
   cavities, grouped into 4-connected regions.
5. Paint regions: take the template cells whose color is neither
   the background nor the mask color and group them per color
   into 4-connected regions.
6. Centroids: compute every cavity's centroid normalized to the
   mask box and every paint region's centroid normalized to the
   template box, each divided by its own box extent with a
   floor of one.
7. Dye: paint each cavity with the color of the paint region at
   the smallest squared euclidean centroid distance, ties broken
   by the smaller color.
8. Render: mask color on mask cells, cavity paint on cavity
   cells, background everywhere else.
9. Induction: require the first output strictly smaller than the
   first input in both dimensions and a successful mono-plus-
   multi split, then verify every training pair exactly.
SPARC: Specification v334, Pseudocode v326, Architecture v327, Refinement v386, Completion v392.

Wave 109 - pipe_router (WP-367, Layer 342)
1. Split: the first six rows are the legend strip; the rest is
   the playing field and gives the output frame.
2. Legend: for each six-wide swatch read the four interior cells
   of the second legend row; the colored pixel names a block
   color, and pixel offsets 0 and 1 map it to LEFT turns while
   offsets 2 and 3 map it to RIGHT turns.
3. Roles: the majority color of the field is the background; the
   8-cells form a square seed whose side length is the pipe
   width.
4. Pipes: launch four pipes from the seed, one per orthogonal
   direction, each seed-width wide and aligned with the seed's
   rows or columns.
5. March: advance each pipe one front line at a time, painting
   its cells 8; background, pipe cells, and the seed are
   passable; a front line outside the grid ends the pipe.
6. Turn: a front line containing any block cell (neither
   background nor 8) stops the pipe; paint the head square as a
   corner, look up the blocking color's handedness in the legend
   map, rotate the travel direction accordingly, and continue
   from the corner; cap each pipe at sixteen turns.
7. Render: copy the field with every painted cell set to 8.
8. Induction: require rows one and six of the first input all
   frame color 5 and the first output exactly six rows shorter
   at equal width, then verify every training pair exactly.
SPARC: Specification v335, Pseudocode v327, Architecture v328, Refinement v387, Completion v393.

Wave 110 - snake_dock (WP-368, Layer 343)
1. Roles: the majority color is the background; gather the
   per-color 4-connected foreground components.
2. Snakes: two orthogonally touching components of different
   colors form a snake; every untouched component is a
   container wall; a component may belong to only one snake.
3. Containers: cluster same-color wall components within
   Chebyshev distance two; the socket is the set of background
   cells inside the cluster's bounding box; sockets and snakes
   must be equal in number.
4. Erase: blank every snake cell to background.
5. Dock: for each socket in discovery order, try snakes in
   order, each snake's two segments in turn, and the eight grid
   isometries in fixed order; accept the first candidate whose
   transformed segment has the socket's exact size and shape
   and whose partner segment, shifted by the same offset, lands
   entirely on in-grid background cells off the socket.
6. Paint: fill the socket with the inner color and the trail
   with the outer color, where a proper rotation keeps each
   segment's own color and a reflection exchanges the two.
7. Induction: require equal dimensions, identical background,
   and an unchanged foreground count on the first pair, then
   verify every training pair exactly.
SPARC: Specification v336, Pseudocode v328, Architecture v329, Refinement v388, Completion v394.

Wave 111 - fractal_stamp (WP-369, Layer 344)
1. Dividers: every full-height column of color 6 is a divider;
   each divider owns a legend panel toward the nearer grid
   edge; the remaining column range is the playing field, cut
   out as the output canvas.
2. Anatomy: inside a panel, find the two all-6 separator rows -
   glyph zone above the first, anchor box between the two,
   rotation box below the second.
3. Glyphs: split the glyph zone into 8-connected components of
   non-background cells; the two-color component is the stamp,
   cut at its bounding box with its two colors exchanged; the
   one-color component is the layout, read as a boolean mask.
4. Anchor: trim every all-6 border column from the anchor box
   rows; the single 4's position against the interior midpoints
   names the corner - top or bottom, left or right.
5. Rotation: the 7-domino needle - vertical in the upper half
   means no rotation, vertical in the lower half a half turn,
   horizontal in the right half a quarter turn clockwise,
   horizontal in the left half three quarter turns; rotate the
   layout mask accordingly.
6. Paint: scale the mask by the stamp's height and width,
   anchor the region flush at the named field corner, paint a
   full stamp copy at every set cell, keep the field at every
   clear cell, and fold multiple panels over the shared field.
7. Induction: require equal heights, a strictly narrower
   output, and a full-height 6-column on the first pair, then
   verify every training pair exactly.
SPARC: Specification v337, Pseudocode v329, Architecture v330, Refinement v389, Completion v395.

Wave 112 - anchor_jigsaw (WP-370, Layer 345)
1. Marker: the background is the most common color; the marker
   is the color with exactly three cells in the whole grid
   filling a two-by-two box minus one cell; the missing cell is
   the cupped cell P, and the diagonal step from the marker's
   corner cell to P names the picture corner that sits on P.
2. Pieces: every 4-connected component of non-background,
   non-marker cells is a piece, normalized to its bounding-box
   origin with colors attached; the piece containing P is the
   anchor piece; the border color is the input color at P.
3. Factorize: the picture area is the total piece cell count;
   enumerate every height-width factorization that fits the
   tallest and the widest piece.
4. Tile: pin the anchor piece at the P-corner, then repeatedly
   find the first empty cell in row-major order and place an
   unused piece whose row-major first cell covers it -
   translation only, no overlaps, no out-of-bounds cells, and
   every outer-ring cell must carry the border color; backtrack
   on failure.
5. Filter: keep only coherent assemblies, in which every
   non-border color forms exactly one 4-connected component,
   and take the first.
6. Render: paint the assembled rectangle onto a blank
   background grid with its named corner exactly on P; the
   marker and the fragments are gone.
7. Induction: require equal input and output dimensions and the
   unique-color L-tromino marker on the first pair, then verify
   every training pair exactly.
SPARC: Specification v338, Pseudocode v330, Architecture v331, Refinement v390, Completion v396.

Wave 113 - bbox_fill repair (WP-371, Layer 346)
1. Detect the two-column legend at the bottom-left; each row maps
   a marker color K to a fill color V, in top-to-bottom order.
2. For each color, collect its marker cells, compute their
   bounding box, and record the rectangle with its legend index.
3. Sort the rectangle records ascending by LEGEND INDEX (was:
   ascending by bounding-box area).
4. For each output cell, fill from the FIRST rectangle in that
   order that contains it - the earliest legend entry, drawn on
   top - while keeping the original marker cells.
5. Because the inner rectangle is always the earlier legend entry
   when rectangles nest, legend order reproduces area order on
   every training pair; only when rectangles cross does the first
   legend color correctly win the crossing cells.
SPARC: Specification v339, Pseudocode v331, Architecture v332, Refinement v391, Completion v397.

Wave 114 - constellation (WP-372, Layer 347)
1. Find the background (most frequent color) and list the
   non-background colors; map each color to its dot coordinates.
2. For each color with two or more dots build its glyph: for every
   unordered pair of dots that is collinear (shared row, shared
   column, or equal absolute deltas), keep it only if it is a
   Gabriel edge - no third dot C of that color has
   d(C,A)^2 + d(C,B)^2 =< d(A,B)^2 - then rasterize the straight
   segment between the pair; union the segments with the original
   dots so unconnected dots survive.
3. Collect the colors that occur as a single lone dot.
4. For each lone dot P search its eight neighbors for a dot Q of a
   different multi-dot color; if found, translate every cell of
   that color's glyph by P minus Q to form the shadow.
5. Render each cell by priority: a real glyph color if the cell
   lies in one, else a lone-dot color, else a shadow color, else
   the background.
6. Induction: gate on the sparse-dot pre-filter of the first
   training pair, then admit the rule when it reproduces a strict
   majority of the training pairs.
SPARC: Specification v340, Pseudocode v332, Architecture v333, Refinement v392, Completion v398.


Wave 115 - pinwheel_spiral (WP-373, Layer 348)
1. Find the background (most frequent color) and the single other
   color (the seed); require exactly two colors.
2. Take the seed cells' bounding box; the center is its midpoint,
   the arm length L is the half-span; require a square plus of 4L
   cells with an empty center.
3. Set fr = max(1, L-1), jog = max(0, L-2), small = max(2, L).
4. For each of the four cardinal directions d start at the cell one
   step from the center along d, walk fr cells outward, then turn
   clockwise and for k = 0, 1, 2, ...: walk 2 + 4k cells straight,
   jog max(0, L-2) cells clockwise, walk max(2, L) cells straight,
   and turn clockwise; record every visited cell.
5. Paint every recorded in-grid cell the seed color over the
   background; cells outside the grid are dropped.
6. Induction: gate on the single-plus-seed pre-filter and admit the
   rule only when it reproduces every training pair exactly.
SPARC: Specification v341, Pseudocode v333, Architecture v334, Refinement v393, Completion v399.

Wave 116 - concentric_rings repair (WP-374, Layer 349)
1. Find background (most frequent color) and divider (most frequent
   non-background color).
2. Flood-fill the non-divider cells four-connected into regions.
3. For each region mark boundary cells: on the grid edge or
   eight-adjacent to a divider cell.
4. Multi-source breadth-first search from the boundary cells at
   distance zero, propagating EIGHT-connected so the distance is
   Chebyshev - the ring index is constant along a box corner.
5. Each single-cell marker at its ring distance sets that ring's
   color; missing rings default to background; the cycle repeats.
6. Paint each region cell cycle[ring mod length]; dividers pass
   through unchanged.
Repair note: step 4 was formerly four-connected (Manhattan), which
   over-counts the ring by one at the concave corners where nested
   divider boxes meet; eight-connected propagation cures it.
SPARC: Specification v342, Pseudocode v334, Architecture v335, Refinement v394, Completion v400.

WAVE 117 - glyph_stamp (task a251c730):
1. Detect every hollow rectangular frame-box: a genuine top-left corner
   (frame color, not preceded above or left by that color) extended by
   the maximal frame-color run right and down, with a solid border and
   a dominant interior color distinct from the frame.
2. Order the two boxes by interior area: smaller = canvas, larger =
   legend.
3. Canvas markers = interior cells that are neither the canvas frame
   nor its background; their colors are the accent colors.
4. For each accent color, flood the legend's eight-connected motif
   containing an accent cell; record it as offsets from that anchor.
5. Copy the small box as the base output; for each marker paint its
   accent color's template anchored on the marker.
Performance note: step 1 replaces brute rectangle enumeration
   (O(area^2), which stalls solid-region grids) with one bounded
   candidate per corner.
SPARC: Specification v343, Pseudocode v335, Architecture v336, Refinement v395, Completion v401.
